B00004BZ16|4.0|The most rehashed line critics use when analyzing The Clash's controversial \\"Sandinista!\\", originally released as a triple-LP following their indisputable masterpiece \\"London Calling,\\" is that somewhere among the original three discs lies a wonderful single-disc. And the great thing about that is, whichever songs you choose to whittle your single helping of the most stunning advances in punk music, there's something for everyone. Most fans will cite the classics contained on \\"Sandinista!\\", usually being 'The Magnificent Seven,' 'Police On My Back,' 'Somebody Got Murdered,' 'Hitsville UK,' and 'Charlie Don't Surf.' But just as well are some incredible Clash gems, all too often glossed over amidst the slew of music the album contains, most notably 'The Street Parade,' 'Washington Bullets,' 'Lose This Skin,' 'Broadway,' 'Junco Partner,' 'Corner Soul,' and 'Kingston Advice.' Or, for the more dedicated - and patient - of fans, there are curios/oddities/throwaways/experiments, whatever cliched adjectives with which the critics like to describe them - such as 'One More Dub,' 'The Sound of Sinners,' 'Shepherds Delight,' 'Version Pardner,' 'Career Opportunities,' 'Mensforth Hill,' and 'Silicone on Sapphire.'<br />Among some of the more difficult - but worthwhile - tracks like 'Junkie Slip,' 'If Music Could Talk,' 'Living In Fame,' or 'Version City,' it seems The Clash and Joe Strummer are trying to express something important, but the message often becomes obscured by the abundance of studio wizardry and multiple musical layers.<br />\\"Sandinista!\\" is, whichever tracks one likes or hates, or even if you hate them all, without question evidence that The Clash were the hardest working punk band of their time. \\"The CNN of punk,\\" as Anthrax guitarist Scott Ian described them. And more impressive is that this triple-album didn't even yield all of the studio output the band produced during this time. With their unblinking political stances added to a myriad of influences and mediums ranging from pop, reggae, rockabilly, funk, gospel, and even children's music, \\"Sandinista!\\" may be a difficult album to accept, but hard evidence as to why The Clash blew every other punk band in existence out of the water.s ranging from pop, reggae, rockabilly, funk, gospel, and even children's music, \\"Sandinista!\\" may be a difficult album to accept, but hard evidence as to why The Clash blew every other punk band in existence out of the water.

B000EXZI1O|5.0|Got to kind of feel for these guys who had to close out the 70's riding high on the overwhelming success of [[ASIN:B000SQFC0Y Saturday Night Fever]]. Suddenly they went from huge to SUPER huge! The end result is they followed this up with another self produced studio album a year and a half later that seems to have gone on to become the bands biggest seller of the decade. One reason for that is pretty clear-their hits were on the radio and in discos everywhere during this time. And because they were the cream of the crop in terms of pop songwriting their high potential for longevity made them idea for long term radio success as well. In the end the setup was about the same as their previous full length studio album: ten songs and a big dance number to start out with. One thing that's to be noticed is the Barry takes about 90% of the vocal leads on this album. His distinctive falsetto became one of the key signatures of the band around this time so they put it to heavy use. But there's something else here as well.<br /><br />  With \\"Tragedy\\",their hit that's most obviously aimed at discos it's apparent what made this album so successful. The production and sound is as glossy and sleek as fiberglass with a coat of red varnish. Basically that means the sound also has this burning fire in it too. Songs such as the pop-funk grooves of \\"Love You Inside Out\\" and \\"Search,Find\\" showcase this on the funkier end of things. There's actually somewhat more ballads on here than is typical for Bee Gee's of this era such as \\"Too Much Heaven\\",\\"Reaching Out\\" and the lightly percussive and folksy title song fitting into that category. \\"Stop (Think Again)\\" is a big orchestrated epic that's something of a modernized take of their orchestral pop/rock sound of the late 60's. \\"Living Together\\" and \\"I'm Satisfied\\" are a bit different than the rest of the music here. These are the two deepest,sparer bass/guitar type funk on an album defined by it's slickness. Robin only gets about 2 1/2 minutes to shine here at the end on \\"Until\\",an amazingly soulful and even jazzy exploration with these warbly,abstract synthesizers.<br /><br />  Following this album the Bee Gee's would change direction during the anti disco freeze out in the early 80's to a full on pop/rock oriented sound. This sadly wouldn't prove very successful for them commercially and it wouldn't be until later in the decade that they'd re-emerge with a sound that could work more successfully for them and their audience. Even still there would always be a little something missing that really only appeared again here. Yes to a point they did get rather typecast with the sound of this era and the pop world never seemed to let go of that. It's sad because with the production,songwriting,vocal and general musical talent these guys possessed I can only imagine what sort of great thing's they'd continued to have come up with if their success wasn't derailed by changing musical tastes and a failed movie experience most people are very familiar with. At any rate this particular album found the Bee Gees still at the top of their form. 0439023521|4.0|There is something infectious about the short, declaratory sentences that open the Hunger Games.  Perhaps it is the indication made so early on and so tacitly that Panem is not a place for deep reflection, a land where long-winded soliloquies are wholly inapproriate and out of place.  Whatever the attraction, this is one of those rare books that snags you at the beginning and doesn't let go until the very end.  It may be impossible to say anything different from what hundreds have already said.  Quite simply put, this is a great book and deserves to be read.<br /><br />The author, Suzanne Collins, does a phenomenal job in crafting a world that is at once engaging, brutal, and terrifyingly possible.  It isn't that the book is so fresh and original that one cannot help but be spellbound, indeed much of what the Hunger Games brings to the table can be found, bit by bit, in other literary works or in films.  That these various elements don't feel trite, however, is a great credit to how wonderfully put together they are.  If the narrative is interesting, I don't particularly care that there may be another book that is somewhat like this one, the book stands on its own two feet and in my estimation is more than original and creative enough.  Arguably one of the author's best decisions was to maintain a fairly rapid pace throughout the novel which kept moments or bits of plot from becoming old too quickly with perhaps a few stumbles here and there (the part where Katniss and Peeta are sitting in a cave comes to mind).<br /><br />Katniss is a good main character and I found it hard not to like her as the protagonist, though at times she seems a little dense which is at odds with 98% of what the book reveals about her.  She's a smart and savvy hunter and can discern the intent behind a sponsor's gift but can't figure out that Peeta isn't lying about his feelings for her.  It makes no sense and is perhaps the only example where the author missed a great opportunity to make her, and that part of the narrative, more three-dimensional and gripping.<br /><br />Of course, the book is \\"brutal\\" insofar as it goes.  I didn't find it to be overly graphic and unlike some others I don't believe in the slightest that the book glorifies or romanticizes violence as there are several instances where characters decry what's going on and express indignation about what they're being forced to do.  The thing to villify is not the PG-13 violence, but the hypothetical governmental forces that not only allow the killing, but compel it to happen.  Those who would see in the book an endorsement of meaningless violence are those that I don't think have really read the book.  You won't receive anything on the order of Golding's Lord of the Flies, but it will force you to ask a meaningful question here and there.  While the book purports to explore the effects of war and violence on those coming of age, it seems that the planned trilogy took precedence and so, maybe, that exploration will be truly started with the second book which might be appropriate since the first one needed to introduce the world and, as I said, it isn't yet one that invites much reflection or philosophizing.<br /><br />Overall, The Hunger Games is a dynamic book that, with a few notable missteps, does a great job in whisking the reader away.  It can be forgiven for being somewhat derivative, if you choose to look at it that way, but it stands as an excellent achievement.  It might not be a true classic but it does leave you hungry for more.
B000EXZI0K|5.0|During the time this album came out I am sure many people aimed as many \\"disco sucks\\" style epithets directly at Barry,Robin and Morris Gibb for \\"going disco\\". Well for one,at the time just about any dance oriented music without a loud guitar was considered disco music. For another it's important to remember that the Bee Gees were a pop band. And that means that their style of music would change often. But their basic handling of melody and vocal harmonies would remain essentially the same. On their previous album [[ASIN:B0063TX06I Main Course]] they recovered from a commercial dry spell with a wonderful,soulful and hit filled album produced by Arif Mardin. He wasn't able to be here so the Bee Gee's decided to do what Hall & Oates would do half a decade later: produce themselves into the charts. The Gibb's certainly had enough musical experience by this time to make self production work for them. And with their new found sense of direction they took their self contained band and delivered an album that I feel is one of if not their strongest overall release.<br /><br />  \\"You Should Be Dancing\\" starts off the album with that heavy,funk fueled afro latin fueled dance track probably indelibly associated with [[ASIN:B000SQFC0Y Saturday Night Fever]] but this is where it originally comes from. Another great part of this album is that it's packed full of undebatable funk such as the sleek sophistifunk of \\"You Stepped Into My Life\\" and the out and out Sly Stone inspired horn funk of \\"Lovers\\" and \\"Boogie Child\\". The latter two songs feature the growling,Boz Scagg's style vocals of Robin and serve as an important reminder Barry's falsetto wasn't the only vocal on Bee Gee records of this era. The band channel Thom Bell style Philly balladry perfectly on \\"Love So Right\\" with Barry's Russell Tompkins like falsetto topping off the creamy music and \\"Love Me\\" and \\"The Way It Was\\" mark the best of their pure pop ballad style. \\"Can't Keep A Good Man Down\\" and \\"Subway\\" showcase a Philly influence though again more in a dance frame of mind. One of the best songs it actually the closing title track,a nice message song starting with a near acappella vocal harmony and diving into a moog bass tinged pop/funk jam with a wonderful melody.<br /><br />  On this album the Bee Gees actually managed to put together the sort of album you can play from beginning to end with no weak tunes. From soul ballads,to funk to grooving pop/R&B this album contains it all. And it actually makes you wonder with it's rich,creamy sonics why the Bee Gees hadn't been self producing their records a lot more. Apparently they'd been taking everything that had been done with previous producers right in and adapting that to help their own inevitable experience when the time arose. Today disco no longer seems to carry the stigma that it used to. As a matter of fact,a lot of people (I am sure including a number of former Bee Gees detractors) have come to realize that the majority of the music on this particular album wasn't aimed at disco dancers at all. 1976 was a very good year in general for soul,funk and R&B. Even the blue eyed variety. If you lined up the works of EWF,Stevie Wonder,P-Funk as well as Boz Scaggs and David Bowie from this era and saw the creative and commercial quality of the music you'd be dealing with...well it's right there for all to see. And I am happy to say the Bee Gee's can add this particular album to that legacy from that year.illy influence though again more in a dance frame of mind. Beach House's music has a very heavy, hypnotizing effect so it takes a few listens to notice the nuances and layers. I found that Bloom is very much a continuation of where they left off with Teen Dream. Generally, I prefer the sound on Teen Dream, but I like what they did on this album in terms of the direction they took with the sound.<br /><br />\\"Wishes\\" is an immediate standout for me, especially with Alex Scally's wonderful guitar break in the middle of the song. \\"Other People,\\" which Beach House has performed while touring for Teen Dream, has a nostalgic sound to it. The chord progressions on it are heartbreakingly lovely, quite like \\"Silver Soul.\\" \\"Myth\\" is also an instant winner - it shares some very similar characteristics with \\"Zebra\\" (including the key), but it is faster and has more sounds in the background. \\"Troublemaker\\" and \\"On the Sea\\" are lovely songs - they form the softer side of the album. \\"On the Sea\\" is to Bloom what \\"Real Love\\" is to Teen Dream.<br /><br />Songs like \\"The Hours,\\" \\"Wild\\" and \\"Irene\\" took me longer to get into. I really like how Victoria does the vocals on \\"The Hours\\" - the way she slides one note to the next while singing the same syllable. I did find the ending of the song a little anticlimactic though. \\"Wild,\\" which for me is the most experimental-sounding song on the record, has easily the biggest-sounding drums of all the songs, but more than that, when the melody grabs you on the line \\"wild in our ways\\" you're basically hooked. \\"Irene\\" is like a slow-burn cousin of \\"10 Mile Stereo\\" with an intense build-up at the end.<br /><br />\\"Lazuli\\" is probably the most progressive song of the record, though it's still very accessible and simple. This song has lots of layers and there's some vocal looping at the end which is very beautiful. \\"New Year\\" is, for me, the weakest song on this album. It's a little too predictable - but I enjoyed the slide effects on the guitar.<br /><br />And for fans of their older stuff, the hidden track at the end of \\"Irene\\" sounds like a leftover track from their first album, with a vintage drum machine sound.<br /><br />I wish Beach House had done something a little different, to surprise us a little bit more. I felt that the songwriting could have been supported with better, even bigger-sounding arrangements, especially with the drums. This is one area where I feel like their attempt to hold on to a classic Beach House sound kind of holds them back a little. Perhaps they wanted to try to sound bigger but still retain a certain tone of intimacy and, I guess, familiarity. Regardless, I definitely enjoyed this album. I have no doubt they'll keep putting out great releases in the future.

And am I the only one who finds his sudden death suspicious? No question he died way before his time (and quite possibly before this book was finished.) Maybe I do suffer from paranoia but I think there are two very suspicious elements of the story here. I've read a lot about this man and the drama surrounding his life. Ever since I read about his reluctance to marry his girlfriend because he feared for her safety against his political enemies, I have thought his premature death due to \\"heart attack\\" was odd. Now my suspicions have grown to include the idea that a ghost writer may have actually written the majority of this novel. I don't doubt Stieg Larsson came up with the idea and probably wrote a vast majority of the text but something never felt right about this third installment.<br /><br />This book is nowhere near as exciting as the first two novels. I kept complaining that this one was pretty boring and it just wasn't the caliber that made the first two so hard to put down. I was literally up each night until three a.m. reading The Girl With The Dragon Tattoo and The Girl Who Played With Fire but The Girl Who Kicked The Hornet's Nest (which is over 800 pages long- a sign that something was different since the others were closer to 300-400 pages long) seemed boring and less focused. The main character Lisbeth Salander spends the majority of this book in the hospital and has virtually no contact with the other main character Mikael Blomkvist. Also the story is so convoluted that I could never remember who was who. I mean why wasn't this book released prior to 2007 or whenever it was released?<br /><br />I guess I am digressing from the review but I think one must take into consideration the possibility that what I am proposing may be true. I think it certainly affects the review of this book. If I am right (and unfortunately we may never know) and Larsson had not died (or possibly been killed) before finishing the book then maybe we would have a better book to review. I gave it three stars in my review because I did enjoy some parts of the book, though the interesting parts took til about page 450-something to get to. B007JM4CWY|5.0|I've played a number of nonogram puzzles on various platforms. While I've only just started with this one, it seems like a good incarnation. The interface is simple and effective. I particularly like that it logically crosses out numbers as you fill the spaces. The hold-sweep move to mark a line of squares is useful as well (and it works for coloring them in, marking as Xs, or erasing as well). The fonts and graphics are very readable.<br /><br />There is one thing you can't do with CrossMe's interface: mark a square as a guess and move forward to see if your guess pans out, with the ability to lock in or revert all those deductions at once. The iOS game \\"Shady Puzzles\\" does an admirable job of this, and even allows up to three nested or parallel guesses. When you get to the more complicated puzzles, you occasionally do need to try out a possibility and see if it leads to a contradiction or not, so I miss this facility. I'm debating knocking a star off my rating for this, but for now, I'll let it stand. CrossMe does seem to have unlimited levels of undo (although no redo), so you can with some care at least explore one guess at a time.<br /><br />As others mentioned, some of the larger puzzles are a bit tricky to fill precisely - you'll be best on a tablet for those, and a stylus certainly wouldn't hurt. However, pinch-zoom is implemented very smoothly, which will let you mark things accurately at the expense of not seeing the whole picture.<br /><br />The tutorial is not particularly good. If you don't know how to play nonograms, you'll be pretty confused. It barely adequately covers the rules, and the one or two strategy tips it offers are confusingly worded. This part of the product could stand to be improved. Still, the gameplay is the thing, so I didn't strike a star from my rating for this.<br /><br />The product description is a bit bit vague about the number of puzzles. When asking the relatively high price of $4.95 for this normally, this is critical information for deciding the value. Anyway, I've gone through each level's selection screen and added them up, and (assuming there aren't any \\"hidden\\" puzzles or other things like that) there are 245 different puzzles here. Only 2 of these are throwaway tutorial levels; they're mostly the real deal. I haven't gone through even the first level yet so I can't say how well the difficulty scales, but I can at least say there's a nice variety in sizes and shapes of grids throughout.<br /><br />Absolutely grab this while it's the Free App of the Day. After that, $4.95 is as I say perhaps a little high, although that still works out to basically $.02 per puzzle so it's a bit miserly to complain. Most of these puzzles will take anywhere from two to 20 minutes to solve; $5 for that much intellectual entertainment really shouldn't be too much to ask.ation for deciding the value. B00828HWJE|4.0|When \\"Dragon Eyes\\" was first announced in the midst of Jean-Claude Van Damme's budding comeback, fans pompously stated that it'd be his definitive reanimation vehicle and was headed for movie theaters. Well, they were wrong on both counts - this one's not about to see the inside of an American theater and it's definitely not a vehicle for Van Damme - but this isn't reason to be disappointed, because despite being a DTV production, it's very good action movie. Not mind-blowingly good (Van Damme's own [[ASIN:B002U6CJCO Universal Soldier: Regeneration]] was superior, if you ask me), but nevertheless one of the better examples out there of quality martial arts flicks being feasible on a relatively small budget.<br /><br />The story: a soft-spoken martial artist (UFC star Cung Le, [[ASIN:B002QW7ALM Pandorum]]) - fresh from prison and the tutelage of his wizened teacher (Van Damme) - seeks to redeem his past by cleaning up a neighborhood sick with drugs, gang violence, and police corruption.<br /><br />As far as Van Damme goes, this movie does in fact mark a new stage in his career: it's the first time he's playing the role of a mentor, which is both satisfying at this point in his career and ironic, since the first time both he and Cung Le were mentioned together, he prophesized hostility between them (see one of his many online interviews in the last three years). Nevertheless, Van Damme's character plays almost entirely in the background and only has one (flashback) scene outside of prison. The movie is thoroughly a vehicle for Cung Le, whose last several years of playing supporting roles effectively bolster him to the status of a respectable action hero. The character he plays isn't particularly intriguing but he's got a fair presence and forcefully pushes most of his opposition aside as a film fighter. Peter Weller drastically steps away from his [[ASIN:B00005N7Z1 Robocop]] legacy to heighten the cast value as a memorable villain, with one of the best interrogation scenes I've seen in a while to his credit.<br /><br />The few reviews I've read about this film take aim at the story; I don't usually argue other peoples' opinions, but seriously - what were you expecting, guys? At any rate, I found no qualm with it: the plot itself is simplistic, but there are a handful of neat twists and character-based surprises to keep things interesting (e.g. Le's character earns control of a Latino gang and makes them surrender their firearms, because \\"Only cowards use guns\\"). With that said, there's one resoundingly weird event that doesn't add up, involving Cung Le's character escaping from a thoroughly impossible situation. Steven Seagal pulled a similar head-scratcher in [[ASIN:B000E6ESD0 Mercenary for Justice]], but Le's unexplained disappearing act takes the cake. How the heck did he put that policeman in the casket? Also, I was sort of disappointed by the ending, but the fact that I had just witnessed some very fine fight scenes helped soften its abruptness. Cung Le isn't Scott Adkins, but he offers an exciting alternative of MMA- and karate-based action. In my experience, mixed martial arts have fared better in Hollywood than low-budget features, but ol' Cung could be the one to even things out with the big leagues. I appreciate the variety of fights, their almost complete lack of one-sidedness, and how well pro fighters like Scott Scheeley and Trevor Prangley made the transition to cinefighting by Le's example. Indeed, the fight between him and the latter name is in the running for \\"brawl of the year\\" as far as I'm concerned.<br /><br />The production isn't perfect, but nevertheless, it's very strong. DTV-isms like computer-edited montages and slow motion scenes exist, but you can almost feel director John Hyams fighting to keep them to a minimum. As much as for Cung Le, this film is a victory for him as well in managing to follow up his abovementioned \\"Universal Soldier\\" movie with a worthy new entry. Plainly said, I'm eager to see what all of these guys get up to in the future, and action fans in general would be in the wrong by not giving this one a serious look.hat all of these guys get up to in the future, and action fans in general would be in the wrong by not giving this one a serious look.

1401923127|3.0|This book's subtitle is Unleashing the Power of Consciousness, Matter & Miracles, so as an avid reader on matters related to spirituality and consciousness, I was excited to read it. The book also had two pages of endorsements within the front cover by several prestigious sources as well as high number of positive reviews on Amazon. I approached my reading with high expectations after such raving reviews.  In the spirit of full disclosure on my mindset for spirituality, I am a firm believer in Original Cause and appreciate scientific theories/studies that harmoniously unite the two mindsets of science and spirituality. I am a also a firm believer that more information should be made available to support their complementary nature as opposed to their segmented viewpoints. I admire and encourage the scientific community that is brave enough to come forward within this context.<br /><br />On the other hand, I am also expect authors to provide at least a thread of content in their book as it relates to the title. I think that perhaps using Understanding instead of Unleashing in the book's subtitle may have been much more appropriate. At the end of the day, I found no content that provided suggestions, theories, practices or methods for Unleashing anything other than a long drawn out and somewhat repetitive explanation of cellular structure and functionality.<br /><br />I consider myself to be fairly smart and I wanted to understand the correlation between the cells, their membranes and how this might all relate to consciousness, but the level of detail that Lipton chose to share in this book was way over the top. Unless this book was intended to be part of the curriculum for a high school or early college biology course, there is just no need to go into the level of specifics about how our cell's amino acids are assembled or providing diagrams on the molecular composition of different protein molecules. I tell you it took every ounce of effort I had and a few cups of coffee to get through the 5 out of 7 chapters in this book that dealt with biological details that I will never remember and that could have been described within a page or two to support the author's viewpoints.<br /><br />I did appreciate the authors attempt to present this dry and specific material in a lighter and conversational manner than most would find in a textbook, but nevertheless the material was extensively detailed for a book that ultimately intended to talk about consciousness and spirituality. I did enjoy the chapter Lipton wrote about Conscious Parenting, entitled: Conscious Parenting: Parents as Genetic Engineers . Don't let the chapter title scare you too much, in this chapter I actually found some theories and studies explained in more general terms which helped to get the authors points across.<br /><br />Some really sour grapes for me where the social statements that were included. I am not a fan of authors using a book to push their social agenda when the book is categorized as something else. Regardless of whether I believe in the social statement or not is not the point. The book is about one thing (according to the title and book description) and should not be used to gather a captive audience to get on a soapbox about some societal issue. If you want to talk about that issue, write a book about it that clearly informs the reader about your content.<br /><br />I'm sure the Lipton intends this viewpoint to be a part of his unleashing of consciousness and a responsible topic to discuss (the statement he is making at the end of the book is about how humans are destroying the earth and each other and we are destined to annihilation if we don't change our conscious behaviors) - but in my viewpoint this is a topic best discussed as part of a venue where your audience is receptive to these viewpoints, not captive. Additionally, what makes this stand out as a social ideological platform rather than a highly generic solution to expanded consciousnesswas the contradictions in his own theories. Either you believe in global limitations (human destruction of the planet) or your believe in cellular infinite adaptation (constantly expanding based on biological and spiritual variables.)<br /><br />For a reader looking to gain insights about how science and spirituality comingle and combine into a harmonious relationship, this book is for you only if you enjoy the high end of the science portion of this equation. For me, someone who enjoys exploring scientific and spiritual concepts and getting background on the concepts presented, this book was way too detailed on the science side of things and very weak on the spirituality side of things. I was able to get his point overall about cellular behavior based on environmental input, but by getting so granular into the science of the cellular structure, I lost interest overall. Frankly, I only finished the book so that I could review it. I would not be able to recommend this book to readers that are interested primarily in consciousness as it relates to both science and spirituality.<br /><br />I did find the writers style and presentment to be easy to read, but if you are presenting material that is dry and over saturating, your casual writing style gets eaten up by your love of hearing yourself talk about details no one cares about or will ever remember (unless you are also a scientist). Finally, the readers do not ever really get a sense of how we might improve our biology of belief, even though the authors states several times we can and that he, in fact, has.was the contradictions in his own theories. 0307951529|4.0|This book could be called the Accidental Startup because some of these business ideas were developed by accident or a result of people making money off a hobby or meeting an unusual unmet need. The examples are inspiring. That's the strength of the book. Anyone can start a business with little or no money. Just setup a fan page on Facebook, get some followers and create products to sell to your fans (that's my idea, not a specific example from the book). I'm always thinking of ideas to make money that start small and I hope my ideas grow to the point where they could make millions. This book definitely inspires me to re-think some of these ideas and not try to plan how I'll make a million but start small and let the process take its course slowly and course correct along the way. If I'm lucky, maybe one or two will be a success.<br /><br />But unfortunately, the book loses focus. In the beginning, the author teases us with the humble origins of some of these businesses and promises that he'll tell us how they got off the ground. But the author starts giving the reader guides on how to get started. As he does that, he sprinkles in an example or two to illustrate his points. Then the reader has to remember or refer back to the tease earlier in the book to put the two parts of the story together. I would have preferred if he talked more about the companies and used their specific story to illustrate certain ideas on how to grow an unusual business idea.<br /><br />For example, I would have liked to learn more about the closeout mattress delivery company. Did he come up with the bike delivery part of the business by accident? How does a person ride a bike with a king sized mattress on it? How do customers react to someone delivering a mattress by bike? What if it rains? How does one person move a mattress from a bike into someone's house? How did he teach potential customers that closeout mattresses were a viable product? Or the piano teacher who developed a schedulingprogram. What program did he need to buy? Did he do the programming or did he hire someone to do it? How much money did he need for the project? How did he get people to accept and buy the software? Or how did the bookkeeper sell her services and compete with all the bookkeeping and accounting firms in her area?<br /><br />If he took the top 25 companies and told the reader how they got past the hurdles from idea to viable businesses, that may have been a better book. But I did like the book and will re-read it and refer back to it for ideas and examples so the business ideas I have in my head might become a reality.

But, since I was a child, I did not know better, so I followed her words and went on the path of freedom. Little did I know that the path of freedom was a path into the dark depths of hell. I went to Harvard at 14 years of age, being the first female ever to be admitted to Harvard at such a young age. I graduated at the age of 20, with a PHD in literature. I began to teach at Harvard, enriching students in my knowledge of lost feminist writings of 5th century Britain. I married at 25 to a brilliant scientist, who quit his career to help raised our two daughters we had a year later. My life would seem ideal to many, but it was far from it. My husband brutalize me by cooking meals for me and my daughters every night, helping my children with their school work, and, at times, tried to romance me into bed, with flowers and \\"I love you's.\\" My professional life was no better. Winning awards, having my research papers of feminist writings in the dead Latin language published was more than I can bear. My life was in utter despair, only made more so whenever I looked at my daughters, knowing that this despair awaited their future. One night, after work, my husband called me and asked (I almost vomited at his, \\"If it is not too much trouble dear; I know how tired you are) if I would go by the bookstore and pick up \\"Goodnight Moon\\" for our youngest daughter's book project. I said yes, not knowing that my life would drastically change. As I enter the bright lights of the bookstore, there display before me was the E. L. James' novel: Fifty Shades of Grey. With the book carefully bathed in the fluorescent heavenly light, I could not resist it's aura. Forgetting my original purpose, I bought the book and immediately took to my car to read it. There, my life changed. E. L. James' writing was unlike anything I have ever read. Her writing lacked the pretentious manner of proper grammar; what a rebel, I thought. But the character of Christen Grey, oh, I came at the very mention of him on every page. He was so unlike any man in my life. He was not a brute like my father or husband. Here was a man, who actually forced his love to have sex with him in the most creative of ways. I felt envious, my husband would never tie me or have violent sex with me, instead, he would only kiss me and make slow love (torture for me) to me with romantic music. But it wasn't just the sex that made me fell in love with Christian Grey. E. L. James showed me a whole new world as to what my life could be. Instead of working hard and making my own decisions, I could have a gorgeous, rich man who could force me into a life of sex and who could make decisions for me. Let me tell you, I nearly bawl my eyes out when he forced Anastasia to work out so she would not gain weight: I learned then what love truly is. Now, I am divorced from my brutal husband and met a new man on suggardaddy.com and he treats me and my daughters well. He forced me to quit my job, have plastic surgery and sex me up every night. Believe me; I have the bruises and scars to prove it. As for my daughters, they still missed their father, even though my new man practically hugs and caress my daughters every day, but I know that I am now providing a better life and future for them. The Gods themselves could have not written a better book! I am so happy thatso many women everywhere are now realizing that we had the path to happiness all along. And may women like Susan B Anthony and Gloria Steinem go rot in the hell that they created for women everywhere!

B0083GQKQG|3.0|Non-linear narratives and hyper-stylized filmmaking seem to be en vogue these days, and unfortunately, they don't always work to a film's advantage. In this case, the director's heavy-handed use of cutaways and jumbled chronology drag down an otherwise brilliant film. (I was reminded, both in methodology and in the use of symbolism, of Lars Von Trier's Antichrist, though mercifully without all the gore.) Tilda Swinton is pitch-perfect as the mother of a young sociopath, and the film wisely refrains from pat judgments or tidy explanations as to whether or not her chilly attitude toward her firstborn affects his descent into evil. For a movie about such horrific events, very little violence is shown on-screen, which makes the climax of the film much more terrifying and effective than a simple bloodbath could have done. All these wisely thought-out decisions make the cumbersome stylistic elements yet more frustrating. This could have been, and should have been, a five star film.
